## Iter 117 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 (115/200) — cto_derek Coding 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate (0114 zero-downtime K8s deployment pipeline), dataraj Data 5-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate (0115 Markov chain multi-touch attribution)

**What shipped.** Two content projects completing the iter 117 target.

**(1) Project 0114** (cto_derek / Coding / intermediate / 4-step / Opus 4.6) — Derek Lawson, CTO of MedAxis (health-tech SaaS for specialty care practices, 38 employees, Series B 8 months prior), fixing a Kubernetes deployment process that was causing 15–45 seconds of HTTP 502s and 503s on every production push and triggering SLA violation notifications from two health-system contracts. Three root causes diagnosed and resolved: **(a)** missing readiness probe — without it, pods entered the GCE LB backend pool immediately on container start rather than after Gunicorn had initialized, causing a 5–15 second window of dropped requests on every rollout; **(b)** no graceful shutdown handling — GCE LB takes 30–60 seconds to drain a backend, but pods were being SIGTERM'd with no preStop delay, causing requests to arrive at a pod that had already closed its listener throughout the drain window; **(c)** migration-before-code sequencing — running Alembic before deploying new pod code meant old pods were running against the new schema for the entire rollout duration, creating a forward-incompatibility window for any migration that changes column nullability or names. Four passes: **(1)** failure mode diagnosis at the LB and pod lifecycle level with the specific mechanism for each of the three errors; **(2)** Kubernetes Deployment manifest update with readiness probe (httpGet /health, initialDelaySeconds: 5, failureThreshold: 3), liveness probe (initialDelaySeconds: 30, conservative restart threshold), preStop lifecycle hook (sleep 15), terminationGracePeriodSeconds: 75 (LB drain window + preStop + buffer), rolling update strategy maxSurge: 1 / maxUnavailable: 0, PodDisruptionBudget minAvailable: 2 with reasoning for each value; **(3)** expand/contract migration pattern with two complete Alembic examples — adding a NOT NULL column (Phase 1: add nullable + write in new code, Phase 2: backfill + constraint after pods cycled) and renaming a column (four phases: add new column + populate, dual-write in code, add NOT NULL after old pods gone, drop old column) — including CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY detail for 2.4M-row production tables and the Alembic transaction context caveat; **(4)** Kubernetes-native canary deployment using label-selector traffic split (3 stable replicas + 1 canary = ~25% traffic, no service mesh required), kubectl scale to zero for instant abort, automated rollback watchdog (Python CronJob checking Datadog error rate against 2% threshold, scales canary to zero and posts to Slack). Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550114`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777114001..114004`; cto_derek author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222209`; Coding category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111104`.

**(2) Project 0115** (dataraj / Data / intermediate / 5-step / Sonnet 4.6) — Raj Patel consulting for Clearfield Software (B2B SaaS no-code analytics, $4.8M ARR, 22 people), replacing last-touch attribution — which was assigning 65% of closed-won revenue to outbound SDR and 3% to content — with a data-driven Markov chain attribution model on 18 months of BigQuery touch event data and 520 closed-won deals. The CMO needed to justify an $80K/year content investment to a CFO who demanded the numbers. Five passes: **(1)** model selection rationale — why Markov chain is the right choice over Shapley value for this dataset size (Shapley requires 2^6 = 64 coalition subsets; at 520 deals many subsets have 2–5 observations, making Shapley estimates high-variance noise; Markov chain requires only sequential transition probabilities, which are estimated from the full path corpus and are low-variance); the removal effect framing (what fraction of conversions would be lost if this channel were removed entirely); one honest caveat (possible intent confounder for content — accounts that seek out content may be higher-intent, meaning some of Markov's content credit may reflect pre-existing intent rather than content's direct influence); **(2)** BigQuery SQL pipeline — 120-day lookback CTE joining marketing_touches to closed-won deals, consecutive same-channel dedup (collapses a 6-email SDR sequence to 1 touch), touch sequence array per deal; four data quality checks: dark-funnel coverage rate (31/520 = 6% deals with no touches, excluded and flagged), path-length distribution, channel exposure rates, channel co-occurrence query revealing 214 deals (43%) with both content and outbound_sdr touches — the relay pattern the CMO described; **(3)** Python Markov chain implementation — build_transition_matrix (transition count dict → row-normalized numpy matrix with absorbing self-loops for CONVERSION/NULL), simulate_conversion_rate (Monte Carlo 50K simulations from START, seed=42 for reproducibility, notes on why Monte Carlo over matrix inversion for sparse matrices), compute_removal_effects (remove each channel from all paths, recompute conversion rate, fractional removal effect normalized to attribution percentage), revenue attribution at avg $9,816 deal ARPA; **(4)** holdout validation framework — chronological 70/30 train/holdout split, score_partial_path function computing Markov-estimated conversion probability from the first half of each holdout deal's path, Spearman correlation of model scores vs path completeness as a proxy (correlation 0.34 achieved, p < 0.001, vs last-touch generating no score for partial paths by construction); CFO confidence framing: "less wrong than last-touch, not proven correct" — last-touch makes a guaranteed wrong assignment for 43% of deals, Markov asks a better counterfactual question; **(5)** 20-minute meeting structure — open with last-touch's broken ruler (not Markov), slide 1 raw path data (43% content exposure, 0% last-touch credit), slide 2 side-by-side model comparison, slide 3 five representative deals, pre-answer the CFO question (holdout validation + "credible range $850K–$1.1M, all above $800K threshold"), recommendation (12x return), CFO test (re-run at Q3 and check if removal effect holds). Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550115`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777115001..115005`; dataraj author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222207`; Data category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111108`.

writing like a press release), structure and length (400–600 words, 7-section skeleton), and the specific framing for a revenue miss that is genuinely not the whole story (name it immediately + mechanism in two sentences + transition to forward reality, not spin); ## Iter 115 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 (111/200) — marcusdev Coding 5-step Opus 4.7 intermediate (0110 custom ESLint plugin), jakefinance Finance 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate (0111 Nashville duplex underwriting)

**(1) Project 0110** (marcusdev / Coding / intermediate / 5-step / Opus 4.7) — Marcus Chen, full-stack developer at a 12-person startup, writing a custom ESLint plugin from scratch to enforce three async/await conventions that kept slipping through code review. He'd never written an ESLint plugin before. Five passes: **(a)** plugin architecture overview — explains ESLint's visitor pattern (meta / create / CallExpression / ArrowFunctionExpression / JSXAttribute / ExpressionStatement node types), why `async` is syntactic (can check `node.async === true` without TypeScript type checker), and priority ordering for three rules: (1) no-async-useeffect first (zero false positives, AST shape is completely distinctive), (2) no-floating-promise-handler second ('warn' severity, some false positives for sync calls), (3) no-then-chain last (most false positives); **(b)** plugin scaffolding — complete directory structure (eslint-plugin-flowco/index.js + rules/ + tests/), package.json with scoped name @flowco/eslint-plugin-flowco, index.js registering all three rules + recommended config, stub rules so plugin loads before logic is written, npm link in npm workspaces context and alternative file: path dependency for monorepos, scoped package naming convention in .eslintrc.json (@flowco/flowco not @flowco/eslint-plugin-flowco); **(c)** rule 1 no-async-useeffect — complete implementation (CallExpression visitor targeting useEffect with async ArrowFunctionExpression or FunctionExpression argument, `callback.async === true` check), explains why the internal-async-function valid case is fine (the useEffect argument is not async, only the nested helper is), 3 valid + 3 invalid RuleTester test suite covering concise async arrow edge case, design note on adding additionalHooks schema option for custom useEffect wrappers; **(d)** rule 2 no-floating-promise-handler — explains the core tradeoff (syntactic-only: fast, some false positives; TypeScript-aware: exact but adds 20-40% lint startup time + @typescript-eslint/utils peer dep), complete syntactic implementation (JSXAttribute visitor matching /^on[A-Z]/ event handlers, checkBody walking BlockStatement looking for ExpressionStatement → CallExpression patterns, explains why AwaitExpression wraps CallExpression so the check is naturally exclusive of awaited calls), 'warn' severity recommendation, void operator as escape hatch; **(e)** CI deployment — GitHub Packages publish with publishConfig + .npmrc + GITHUB_TOKEN token scope (write:packages), file: path vs npm link resolution for monorepos, GitHub Actions lint.yml with setup-node registry-url + scope + NODE_AUTH_TOKEN: GITHUB_TOKEN (built-in secret, no setup required), husky init + lint-staged with *.{ts,tsx} → eslint --fix --cache, --max-warnings=0 for CI but omitted from lint-staged (let warns through at commit, catch in CI), versioning convention for CHANGELOG.md. inspection strategy: general inspector $350-500 + separate HVAC tech $150-250 = cheap information relative to risk); **(d)** offer recommendation — concrete call: offer $375,000 with $3,000 closing cost concession + separate $7,500 ask on Unit B HVAC (documented inspection finding; price reduction preferred over concession to reduce principal), water heater $1,500 credit, inspection contingency 10 days, financing contingency, 42-day close; at $375K: loan $281,250, P&I $1,872 vs $1,947, effective housing cost drops to $1,075/month; Cap Rate rises to 4.93%; walk threshold if seller holds firm above $383K with no HVAC concession; equity upside frame: 4% appreciation ($15,000) + $3,100 principal paydown + $11,040 housing savings = ~$29,000 year-1 economic gain on $103,000 cash invested = 28% economic return. ## Iter 114 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 (109/200) — sarahgrows Marketing 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate (0108 B2B referral program), teacherben Education 3-step Opus 4.7 beginner (0109 6th-grade argument writing rubric)

**(1) Project 0108** (sarahgrows / Marketing / intermediate / 4-step / Opus 4.6) — Sarah Mitchell, marketing consultant embedded at Flowline (B2B project management SaaS for creative agencies, 480 paying accounts, ACV ~$3,600, CAC $1,200), building the company's first customer referral program after the CEO set a target of 15% of new ARR from referral within 12 months. Constraints: no standalone referral tool budget, just Customer.io, Stripe, and in-product notifications. Four passes: **(a)** program mechanics design — argues against making all 480 accounts eligible at launch (60-day tenure + 2 team members threshold = ~144 eligible accounts, the 30% with real results to share); cash-over-credit incentive rationale ($200 Stripe payout to referrer, 2 months free to referred account = effective referral CAC of ~$800 vs current $1,200 paid CAC, 33% improvement); in-product trigger design at three satisfaction-signal moments (project completion, deliverable export, 10-project milestone) rather than email blast; abuse prevention stack (domain-match self-referral block, 90-day code expiry, 30-day payout hold, 10-payout-per-year cap); explicit list of what not to build at launch (portal, leaderboard, multi-tier structure); **(b)** in-product copy — "warm introduction over cold marketing" principle; modal copy surfacing project name for personalization; pre-filled referral email at 50 words that reads like a real peer message ("Hey, our team has been using this for client projects — thought you'd like it"); referred-account email surfacing referrer name+company as the trust mechanism; implementation note to put the pre-filled email in an editable textarea before send rather than firing automatically; **(c)** launch email — subject "We're paying you $200 to tell a friend" with rationale (naming the incentive in the subject vs "Introducing our referral program" consistently outperforms); from-name Sarah Mitchell not "Flowline Team"; email under 200 words with direct voice ("I'm going to keep this direct"); Customer.io segmentation spec (created_at < today-60d AND team_member_count >= 2 AND status=active); **(d)** 90-day measurement plan — three-layer metric stack: Layer 1 program activity (send rate ≥25%, link click rate ≥40%, trial start rate from click ≥35%), Layer 2 business conversion (referral trial-to-paid ≥35% vs baseline, referral CAC vs $1,200 benchmark, referral ARR contribution toward 15% target), Layer 3 sustainability (payout timing as trust metric, referrer repeat rate 15–25% target, referrer retention delta vs non-referrers); interpretation of early numbers (22 sends → 11 clicks = 50% click rate above target, 11 clicks → 3 trials = 27% trial start rate below target — suggests post-click landing experience needs investigation); day-90 decision framework with explicit shut-down / double-down / redesign criteria and thresholds. Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550108`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777108001..108004`; sarahgrows author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222202`; Marketing category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111102`.

**(2) Project 0109** (teacherben / Education / beginner / 3-step / Opus 4.7) — Ben Okafor, 6th-grade ELA teacher, building a standards-aligned argument writing rubric for CCSS.W.6.1 after finding that online rubrics were either too complicated for students to read or too vague to generate useful diagnostic data. Three passes: **(a)** rubric design rationale — five-category structure (Claim, Evidence+Reasoning, Counterclaim, Organization, Language+Conventions) with explanation of why Counterclaim gets its own row (W.6.1b requirement + students treat it as optional unless graded separately); "Proficient / Approaching / Emerging / Beginning" over "Excellent / Good / Fair / Poor" with rationale (descriptive-progress labels tell students what the gap is; comparative labels tell them how they rank); explains why both goals — diagnostic precision and student-readable clarity — are in tension and how to balance them; 4-point-per-category / 20-point-total scoring with argument against weighting at launch; **(b)** full rubric — all five categories, all four levels, each descriptor written to describe "what is on the page," short sentences, no SAT vocabulary, with a specific note that the Counterclaim "Approaching" row ("mentions the opposing view but does not respond to it") will catch ~60% of the class and names it as a teaching-problem not a rubric-problem, enabling a 5-minute targeted mini-lesson rather than 20 individual paper comments; scoring bands with reteach guidance; **(c)** student self-assessment checklist (11 checkbox items, present-tense active language, with a "what to do before submitting" action item for the most common counterclaim gap) and model evidence+reasoning paragraph (University of Houston uniform study, annotated with Evidence sentence → "This matters because…" → "This shows that…" scaffold, with a note that the reasoning sentences are intentionally longer than the evidence sentence and that this ratio is correct and should be surfaced explicitly). Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550109`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777109001..109003`; teacherben author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222205`; Education category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111106`.

## Iter 113 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 (107/200) — dataraj Data 5-step Opus 4.6 intermediate (0106 churn survival analysis), lena_solopreneur Strategy 4-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate (0107 competitive intel workflow)

**What shipped.** Two content projects completing the iter 113 target.

**(1) Project 0106** (dataraj / Data / intermediate / 5-step / Opus 4.6) — Raj Patel, data analyst consultant embedded at Canopy (B2B project management SaaS for architecture and engineering firms with 400 accounts and two CSMs), building a Cox proportional hazards churn prediction system after the head of revenue identified that churned accounts had gone quiet 60-90 days before renewal and the existing informal system — whoever is loudest gets attention — was systematically missing them. Five passes: **(a)** Cox vs logistic regression trade-off analysis — answers the "strictly better" misconception by framing the genuine difference (logistic answers "will this account churn within N days?"; Cox answers "what is the instantaneous hazard rate, and what is the conditional survival probability to any future date?"), explains where Cox adds genuine value (censored observations, conditional survival output, time-varying covariates), recommends building logistic regression as a baseline first then comparing, notes the PH assumption and the "time at risk = contract start not signup" gotcha, recommends Cox for the renewal-cycle conditionality output but not as a skip-the-baseline shortcut; **(b)** feature engineering from four Postgres tables (accounts, events, support_tickets, billing) — full feature extraction SQL with parameterized snapshot date, usage recency (days since last activity + days since last project created), active user counts in L28 vs P28 windows for slope detection, distinct feature types as breadth proxy, usage ratio for trajectory direction, plus support and billing CTEs (high-priority ticket count, late payment indicator), derived columns recommended for Python (active_user_decline, days_to_renewal, tenure_days), deprioritizes NLP on tickets and event-type frequency distributions, flags label imbalance and recommends precision-at-top-K over overall AUC; **(c)** Cox model with lifelines — complete Python implementation including NaN imputation (median for continuous, 0 for binary), StandardScaler (required because Cox is not scale-invariant), CoxPHFitter with L2 penalizer=0.1 (important for stability with 400 accounts), proportional_hazard_test with rank time transform, hazard ratio summary with 95% CI sorted by HR, and per-account CSM-facing output using conditional survival P(survive to T+horizon | survived to T) — explains why conditional rather than unconditional survival is the correct framing for long-tenured accounts; **(d)** threshold calibration — cost-weighted analysis (false negative ~$2,400 in expectation vs false positive ~$25 = ratio of 96, theoretically push threshold very low), explains why the binding constraint is CSM buy-in not the loss function (if 20 of 21 proactive calls go nowhere CSMs stop trusting the model), recommends capacity-aware dynamic threshold: top-K by score with a min_score floor (0.20) rather than fixed scalar, adds days_to_renewal 30-180 day filter to prevent flagging accounts too early for a renewal conversation; **(e)** weekly dbt model and Slack alert — dbt SQL model (materialized as table, tagged weekly, base account filter to renewals 30-180 days out, usage/support/billing CTEs with COALESCE nulls to sensible defaults, DATEDIFF and ZEROIFNULL for Snowflake dialect) plus complete Python scoring script (Snowflake connector, lifelines predict_survival_function with conditional survival loop, top-K filter, Slack SDK chat_postMessage with account-by-account risk lines), advises pickle reuse with monthly refit rather than weekly to avoid small-sample model drift. Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550106`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777106001..106005`; dataraj author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222207`; Data category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111108`.

**(2) Project 0107** (lena_solopreneur / Strategy / intermediate / 4-step / Sonnet 4.6) — Lena Morales, solopreneur running Zestful (a Notion-based freelancer personal finance tool at $14/month), building a systematic competitive intelligence workflow after discovering — two months after the fact — that Bonsai had launched a free tier limited to three active clients, which had quietly eaten her trial conversions in the 2-3 client segment. Exit surveys reported "found a free option" but she had no monitoring system to catch the move proactively. Four passes: **(a)** competitive landscape mapping — 90-minute one-time protocol (Google search strings, Product Hunt with 24-month filter, Reddit r/freelance + r/personalfinance search, G2/Capterra sort by most recently reviewed, Gumroad/Etsy direct competitor set, own exit surveys as best signal for what competes at the decision moment), three-tier classification (Direct / Adjacent / Emerging), five signal categories with check frequency (pricing changes and feature announcements weekly; messaging changes, review volume, and job postings monthly), four-rule action filter keyed to whether intel changes the conversion decision, the positioning, the product backlog, or nothing that needs action; **(b)** free monitoring stack — exact configuration for four tools: Google Alerts with quoted competitor name + pricing/free-tier search strings on weekly digest delivery, Visualping on competitor pricing pages (5 free monitors, explains this is the tool that would have caught Bonsai's free tier launch), Product Hunt topic follows with Freelance/Finance/Productivity, monthly manual G2 review velocity check; Friday 25-minute review routine with time allocations and a decision gate ("did anything trigger Category 1?") that prevents research sprawl; **(c)** decision-oriented competitive matrix — three-worksheet structure built backward from pricing decisions: Sheet 1 pricing/conversion table (free tier + limits + paid entry + trial length, filled example showing Zestful is the only direct competitor without a free tier), Sheet 2 positioning/messaging table (who they say it's for + core value prop + G2 complaints, designed to surface the "too complex for beginners" gap across Bonsai and Wave), Sheet 3 minimal feature parity checklist (8-10 features sourced from own support tickets not a textbook feature list), explains how each sheet answers a different pricing decision rather than being a comprehensive inventory; **(d)** positioning decision — four-part recommendation: (i) drop price from $14 to $12 (price-parity with Solo.app, the closest structural competitor, compete on simplicity not price), (ii) free-forever tier at one active client with no trial clock (directly addresses the Bonsai overlap and removes the conversion barrier for the 1-client segment), (iii) extend paid trial from 14 to 21 days to catch the second invoice cycle, (iv) add basic quarterly tax estimation (most-requested feature, present in 3 competitors); messaging shift to "simple-first freelancer finance for first 1-3 years of self-employment" with "The simplest way to track your freelance money. Free for your first client." as directional tagline; execution sequence: price drop and trial extension this week (config changes, one day), free tier build over two weeks, tax estimation as Q2 milestone, messaging update only after product matches it; notes Notion-native positioning as a genuine differentiator not to dilute. Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550107`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777107001..107004`; lena_solopreneur author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222210`; Strategy category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111109`.

"Competing Against Luck" (2016).

## Iter 112 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 (105/200) — ops_nina Productivity 4-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner (0104 async comms protocol), priya_creates Design 8-step Opus 4.7 advanced (0105 design system governance)

**What shipped.** Two content projects completing the iter 112 target.

**(1) Project 0104** (ops_nina / Productivity / beginner / 4-step / Sonnet 4.6) — Nina Kowalski, operations manager at a 50-person remote agency eight months into full distribution, building a complete async communication framework after the team developed chronic urgency-ambiguity: late-night Slack pings, two standups turned into status-report sessions, senior designers blocking calendars to get deep work done. Four passes: **(a)** diagnostic audit framework — 8-question 20-minute team lead interview to surface friction patterns rather than general complaints (failure-mode story, volume baseline, urgency-gap question, default-behavior question, implicit-pressure-from-late-messaging question, @here usage question, interrupt-type classification, ideal-state question), plus a three-question sync-vs-async decision tree based on the principle "urgency is defined by the sender's progress being blocked, not the sender's anxiety"; **(b)** one-page async protocol document — channel taxonomy table (updates/discussion/project/DM/email/video call with Use For and Not For columns), response time SLAs per channel (4h for discussion and DM, same-day email, 2h for @here, 4h for @channel), firm after-hours rule (messages sent after 6pm carry no response expectation until the following morning, Do Not Disturb is expected behavior not optional), and a three-criterion meeting test (real-time back-and-forth required + right people available without disruption + outcome couldn't be reached async); **(c)** weekly project card template — six fields (shipped this week / in progress with progress markers / decisions needed with deadline and owner / blockers / risks / needs a live sync), with fill-time calibration targeting 10–15 minutes and read-time under 5 minutes, and design note explaining that the "decisions needed" field is the structural replacement for the Monday kick-off meeting; **(d)** rollout email and one-page cheat sheet — email under 400 words explaining the why, what changed, what didn't, and one concrete behavior for week one ("before you send a DM, ask if it blocks real work today"); cheat sheet compressing the decision tree, channel SLAs, after-hours rule, and project card fields onto a single scannable page. Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550104`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777104001..104004`; ops_nina author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222206`; Productivity category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111107`.

**(2) Project 0105** (priya_creates / Design / advanced / 8-step / Opus 4.7) — Priya Sharma, senior UX designer at Fintrek (a B2B fintech SaaS building dashboard and reporting tools for finance teams), building a complete design system governance framework after the team grew from 2 to 12 designers in 18 months and the component library fragmented — four versions of Button in production, zero documentation explaining canonical versions or why forks happened, three 1:1 explainers per new hire. Eight passes: **(a)** component audit methodology — three-phase audit (inventory spreadsheet with instance count + variant count + version history; A/B/C drift classification where A = intentional and documented, B = intentional but undocumented, C = accidental fork; severity scoring using Impact × Divergence + Engineering Cost with sprint-one targets at 7–11); **(b)** three-tier component classification taxonomy — Tier 1 Foundation (atoms, brand tokens, no forking, used 10+ screens), Tier 2 Pattern (molecules, recurring problems, 3+ product areas, changes require review), Tier 3 Template (pages/sections, product-specific, freely customizable), with promotion criteria and multi-brand note explaining why semantic tokens must land before Q3 multi-brand work; **(c)** two-tier token architecture — primitive tokens (raw values, not used in components directly) vs semantic tokens (design decisions, role-named, brand-specific mapping), naming convention (category-role-modifier with hyphens), six-month migration sequence (primitive layer first → semantic mapping → Tier 1 migration starting with Button and Input → brand B validation → Q3 multi-brand launch), plus the migration gotcha about primitive tokens used for non-brand purposes requiring an audit pass during month 3–4; **(d)** Button component documentation as the reference template — Overview, Anatomy, Variants table (Primary/Secondary/Ghost/Destructive with use/not-use conditions), Sizes (Large/Medium/Small with height and use case), States (default/hover/active/focus/disabled/loading with focus ring and disabled semantics guidance), Token references table per variant, Accessibility (touch target, contrast, aria-live for loading, tabIndex for disabled), Do/Don't, Related components, and Changelog; **(e)** governance RFC — committee structure (2–3 senior designers rotating quarterly + engineering rep + ops facilitator, ~2h/week, bi-weekly 30-min sync, Tier 3 explicitly excluded from committee scope), three-stage contribution process (propose with 30-min async request → build to spec → 45-min library review), breaking change policy (committee approval + minimum 2-week sunset timeline + migration guide written before change ships + Deprecated status before removal), with a "what this costs vs what the current system costs" section designed to frame governance as relief not overhead; **(f)** ADR-style design decision log — five-field template (context / decision / rationale / consequences / superseded by) plus a fully worked example DDL-0004 (Button border-radius stays at 0px: two-client sample not a usability finding, cascade decision would require migrating all interactive elements, sharp corners are a deliberate brand differentiator, alternative "optional rounded theme variant" rejected due to parallel token set maintenance and visual inconsistency across client instances, revisit trigger defined at 3+ client requests in one quarter); **(g)** contributor guide — how the library is organized (tier descriptions), three-step check before building (Figma search + doc pages + #design-system question), contribution request format (4 fields), build checklist (states + tokens + mobile + accessibility + doc + changelog), review submission, and the "rough edges" note explaining that silent fixes to existing Tier 1/Tier 2 components create undocumented changes and must go through the contribution process even when the fix is clearly correct; **(h)** Q2 roadmap with OKRs — three objectives (resolve component drift / launch governance / begin token migration) each with measurable key results (severity-8+ consolidation done, zero new forks, 5 component docs published; committee formed, 2 contributions through new process; primitive and semantic layers defined, 2 components migrated to semantic tokens), prioritized work items with week-level timeline, dependency note (migrated components should be consolidated canonical versions), and a "what success looks like" close framing the outcome in terms useful to product and engineering stakeholders. Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550105`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777105001..105008`; priya_creates author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222204`; Design category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111105`.

## Iter 111 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 (103/200) — jakefinance Finance 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate (0102 angel investing), cto_derek Coding 7-step Opus 4.7 advanced (0103 OpenTelemetry distributed tracing)

**What shipped.** Two content projects completing the iter 111 target.

**(1) Project 0102** (jakefinance / Finance / intermediate / 4-step / Opus 4.6) — Jake Torres, CPA with an $80K brokerage account and zero angel investing experience, working through a $25K SAFE offer from his friend Liu Yang, CEO of Stackify (a B2B workflow automation tool for small marketing agencies, raising $1.2M pre-seed). Jake wanted to think through the investment like an investor, not a friend. Four passes: **(a)** evaluation rubric for pre-seed stage — five dimensions in order of signal strength (founder judgment on specifically-named past failure > market wedge clarity > early customer behavior > product defensibility > financial terms), with specific questions to bring to Liu and what each answer would tell him about the investment; **(b)** SAFE terms analysis — $8M post-money cap is defensible for a pre-revenue B2B SaaS in a clearly defined niche (at Series A at $20M pre-money, $25K converts to 0.3125% before dilution; at $100M exit that is a 12.5x gross return), 20% discount is market standard and unremarkable, MFN clause is investor-protective and standard, but the missing pro-rata right means Jake has no mechanism to maintain ownership percentage in a future round and should negotiate for one before signing; **(c)** portfolio construction for a first-time angel — $25K represents 31% of available brokerage capital, which is 3× the maximum per-position check size if you want a properly diversified portfolio of 10+ investments, meaning Jake is either making a concentrated one-time bet on a personal relationship (not building a portfolio) or should reduce to $8–12K per position; **(d)** decision memo — go at $15K with two conditions (pro-rata right negotiated in, check size reduced from $25K to $15K to leave capital for a second angel investment within 12–18 months), formatted as a one-page memo with company description, why this team, investment thesis, key risks, decision and terms, and early warning signals for year one. Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550102`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777102001..102004` (4-step, projects-100-199 convention); jakefinance author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222203`, Finance category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111101`.

**(2) Project 0103** (cto_derek / Coding / advanced / 7-step / Opus 4.7) — Derek Lawson, CTO at Delphi Health (a health-tech startup running a 5-service Node.js microservices platform on ECS Fargate), retrofitting distributed tracing after a P95 latency regression on POST /appointments went from 180ms to 620ms two months after shipping a multi-provider scheduling feature. Three weeks of CloudWatch guessing produced nothing; distributed tracing found the root cause in one session. Seven passes: **(a)** tool selection — full comparison of OTel+Grafana Tempo vs Datadog APM vs AWS X-Ray for their specific stack (Node 20, Express, pg, Redis, ECS Fargate, existing Grafana instance), recommendation for OTel+Tempo on cost (under $50/month vs $155+/month for Datadog), vendor neutrality, and native Grafana integration; **(b)** SDK bootstrap — complete tracing.ts with NodeSDK, OTLPTraceExporter, BatchSpanProcessor, auto-instrumentations disabling noisy fs/net/dns, SIGTERM flush handler, ECS sidecar Collector task definition JSON, and minimal collector.yaml with OTLP receiver → batch processor → otlp/tempo exporter; critical require-first constraint explained (import './tracing' must be the first line in index.ts, before Express or pg load); **(c)** context propagation — explains why two-service traces appear as separate root traces (only one service instrumented; provider-svc starts new root span because it cannot read the W3C traceparent header), fix is instrumenting provider-svc with the same SDK, verification with a manual traceparent curl, roll-out order for the remaining three services; **(d)** custom span attributes — request-level middleware pattern for appointment_type and a hashed patient_id (SHA-256 + secret server-side salt so the hash is consistent across requests for debugging but not reversible without the salt, addressing the HIPAA exposure risk of raw PHI in trace data), inline tracer.startActiveSpan for the slot_availability_check span with scheduling.attempt_count / slot_query_window_days / provider_count / slots_found; **(e)** tail-based sampling strategy — explains why head-based 10% sampling drops 90% of errors (wrong), recommends AlwaysOn SDK with OTel Collector tail_sampling processor: always-keep-errors + always-keep-high-latency (threshold 400ms) + always-keep-retries (attempt_count 2+) + 15% probabilistic baseline; storage estimate (56,000 spans/day at 100% → ~11,760 spans/day sampled = ~700MB/month at S3 rates); Collector RAM sizing (2GB minimum, monitor drop counter); **(f)** Grafana dashboard + alert — architecture explanation (Tempo queries cannot drive alert rules; need spanmetrics processor to generate Prometheus histograms), complete collector.yaml spanmetrics + prometheus exporter config, four-panel dashboard (service error rate stats, P50/P95/P99 latency timeseries, top slow operations table, recent high-latency traces Tempo panel), alert rule at 0.4 seconds (not 400 — Prometheus uses seconds) with 5-minute for-condition to filter transient spikes; **(g)** root cause diagnosis and fix — trace waterfall shows 28 pg.query child spans at 9–14ms under slot_availability_check, identified as N+1 (one query per provider in a loop), fixed with a single `SELECT ... WHERE ps.provider_id = ANY($1::uuid[])` batched query using the PostgreSQL ANY operator (safe array parameter, no dynamic IN clause), P95 drops to ~185ms, verification by querying slot_availability_check spans post-deploy and confirming child span count drops from 28 to 1, three follow-up actions (query count assertion in integration tests, scheduling.db_query_count span attribute for early detection, patient-records service audit for the same pattern). Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550103`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777103001..103007` (7-step); cto_derek author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222209`, Coding category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111104`.

**Why this approach (rationale).** Two constraints drove the project choices for iter 111. First, project 0102 was already drafted (unstaged changes from a prior run that did not commit): jakefinance angel investing was the top of the iter 110 follow-up candidate list, Opus 4.6 was within-1 on model balance (34/33/33 after iter 110), Finance was an appropriate category for jakefinance, and the chain topic (SAFE evaluation + portfolio construction + decision memo) generates genuinely distinct deliverables at each of four steps without any step being derivative. The 7-step tail was at 4 after iter 110 (7-step and 8-step each at 4); advancing to 5 is meaningful chain-length diversity. Opus 4.7 for project 0103 restores perfect 34/34/34 three-way model balance after iter 110 left it at 34/33/33. Distributed tracing as a topic is a genuine gap in the corpus: cto_derek's existing chains cover PHI data boundary RFC, production webhook delivery, and API security — none of them covers observability instrumentation from scratch, and the "what tool to choose + how to set it up + how to actually use it to find a bug" arc is the most realistic version of how engineering CTOs actually use Claude for these decisions. ## Iter 110 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +1 (101/200) + production-readiness (corpus sequence audit)

**What shipped.** Two deliverables: **(1) Project 0101** (emwriter / Writing / intermediate / 5-step / Sonnet 4.6) — Emily Zhao, freelance content strategist and ghostwriter, building a complete crisis communications package on a Sunday morning after a client (Marcus Reyes, founder of Harvest + Table, a D2C meal kit company with 8,200 subscribers) called her with a food safety recall situation. Their February Harvest Bowl kit — lot HT-FEB-2024-A, shipped to 4,100 customers in 23 states — contained a Golden Sesame Sauce with undisclosed cashews (supplier substituted a cashew-based tahini alternative without notification; allergen label listed sesame only). Two customers reported reactions, one requiring an EpiPen. Lawyer and insurance already engaged. Emily had roughly 18 hours to build the full comms package before word spread. Five passes: **(a)** crisis framework — correct stakeholder notification sequence (affected customers first → FDA voluntary notification → broader subscriber base → press/media → support team before phones start, with explicit reasoning for each order decision), three message pillars (factual transparency about the specific allergen, clear actionable steps for the customer, accountability at the company level not transferred to the supplier), and a six-phrase strike-list with explanations of why each backfires ("no serious injuries reported" — the EpiPen use is an adverse event and the scope is unknown; "this situation" as a euphemism for the word recall; "we take food safety very seriously" — content-free template phrase; "due to an isolated supplier error" — leads with blame-shifting against Pillar 3; "we apologize for any inconvenience" — wrong register for an allergen reaction; "we have no reason to believe" — speculation); **(b)** customer recall email — 310-word email to 4,100 affected recipients with subject line "Important: allergen alert for your February Harvest Bowl kit — please read," preheader leading with the allergy action not brand voice, body structured as what-happened / what-this-means-for-you / how-to-check-lot-number / three-action-steps (set sauce aside, submit return at harvestandtable.com/recall, contact if reacted), and personal closing note from Marcus written as a person who is distressed not as a legal-reviewed signoff; **(c)** social media statements — 280-word Instagram caption leading with allergen alert (not brand voice), then full recall explanation, then what happened with the supplier, then apology — and a three-tweet thread that compresses to: alert + link / refund + reaction contact / what happened + audit timeline; **(d)** AP-style press release — full press release attributed to Marcus Reyes as founder, facts-only (lot number, product name, 4,100 units, 23 states, two known adverse reactions acknowledged without personal disclosure, supplier substitution without notification), company instructions to affected customers, and 30-day audit follow-up commitment; **(e)** customer support Q&A — 10 scenarios for three part-time reps with no prior recall experience, formatted for scanning during a live call: ate it/no symptoms, child ate it with pediatrician+911 routing, do-I-need-a-doctor deflection to medical provider, had-a-reaction/EpiPen immediate-transfer-to-Marcus (no asking for details, document name and callback), why-wasn't-I-notified-sooner (corrects the premise without apologizing for wrong timeline), what-happened-with-the-supplier (fact-only, no speculation about consequences), compensation-beyond-refund (route to Marcus, document, no promises), media-inquiry-wrong-line (media contact + offer to send release, no additional answers), never-got-the-email (account lookup + offer to resend), already-threw-it-away (no return required for refund). Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550101`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777101001..101005` following the projects-100-199 convention; emwriter author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222208`, Writing category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111103`. **(2) Production-readiness: corpus sequence audit** — verified that all 101 project UUIDs from `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550001` through `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550101` are present in seed-content-chains.sql with no gaps. Python one-shot confirmed each of the 99 legacy UUIDs (0001–0099) individually. Projects 0100 and 0101 verified separately. No out-of-sequence IDs detected. Step UUID count for project 0101 confirmed at 5 (`grep -c`). Total `$pf$` token count post-insert: 3,952 (up from 3,914 by exactly 38: project INSERT 4 fields × 2 = 8, five steps × 3 fields × 2 = 30; 38 total, even = all pairs balanced).

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 109's follow-up (d) explicitly named "emwriter (book proposal structure / corporate comms for a product recall)" as a fresh candidate for iter 110 and noted that emwriter's existing corpus (B2B fintech launch post, all-hands letter after missed quarter, legacy editor sunset announcement) is entirely outbound or change-communication work — none of it is crisis communication. A product recall is fundamentally different: it involves safety, legal context, regulatory actors, a compressed timeline, and five distinct communication formats (customer email, social, press release, CS Q&A, and the strategy framework that scaffolds all of them). The chain topic generates genuinely distinct deliverables at each of five steps, with each step building coherently on the prior — the framework is the backbone, the customer email is the first use of it, the social statements are constrained by "email sends confirmed first," the press release is triggered by journalist outreach, and the Q&A is the last piece needed before Monday. Chose Sonnet 4.6 because: crisis communications is structured reasoning about audience, sequence, and tone — not multi-variable technical analysis; Sonnet handles communication strategy and draft writing well at this quality bar; model balance was at 33/33/33 after iter 109 and any model was valid, so picking by topic fit rather than by balance pressure. Chose Writing category over Strategy because: the primary deliverables are all communication artifacts (email, social, press release, Q&A) — strategy is the upstream scaffolding that makes them better, but the category tag should reflect what someone browsing "Writing" would expect to find. Chose 5-step intermediate over alternatives: the topic has exactly five distinct phases (framework → customer email → social → press release → CS Q&A) that do not compress or combine naturally; intermediate is correct because a first-year communications person could follow the chain but would miss the judgment calls (why customer-first before social, why not lead with supplier context, why the EpiPen use disqualifies "no serious injuries") without explanation. Alternatives considered: jakefinance for a cap table mechanics / angel investing chain (Finance, would continue the jakefinance corpus well) — rejected because Finance has had recent iterations (0096, iters 107–108) and Writing has not been touched since iter 105 (0093); a 7-step cto_derek chain for distributed tracing to advance the thin tail — rejected because this iteration's production-readiness constraint (1 content + 1 prod-readiness) limits time and the 5-step crisis comms chain is fully at-depth without crowding the iteration. Production-readiness choice (corpus sequence audit): iter 109's ITERATION_LOG identified "corpus sequence audit (confirm no out-of-order project IDs or UUID gaps)" as the highest-priority remaining production-readiness task. A gap or duplication in the UUID sequence would produce silent INSERT conflicts in Postgres (ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING or duplicate-key errors depending on the RLS policy) — worth verifying before the corpus grows to 200 and becomes harder to audit. The audit completed clean: all 0001–0101 present, no gaps.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — no external WebFetch required per SKILL.md. Real-world grounding for project 0101: the FDA's voluntary recall notification path is documented in the FDA's "Recalls, Market Withdrawals, & Safety Alerts" guidance — companies are expected to notify FDA within 24 hours for Class I recalls (potential serious health consequences) and can self-initiate via MedWatch or the district office; the CDC and FDA both document the regulatory framework under 21 CFR Part 7 for voluntary food safety actions; tree nut allergy cross-reactivity (cashews cross-react with pistachios; neither typically cross-reacts with sesame) is documented in FARE (Food Allergy Research & Education) allergen guides; EpiPen use is a proxy for anaphylaxis which the FDA classifies as a serious adverse event under 21 CFR 310.305 / 314.81; the "notification sequence" principle (direct customer notification before public posting) is a standard PR crisis management principle covered in sources including the Edelman Crisis Communications guides and the PRSA crisis practice guides; the "we take food safety very seriously" phrase is a documented example of empty crisis communication language cited in multiple crisis comms training programs; the "no serious injuries have been reported" phrase is specifically flagged in food safety crisis communication training as factually hazardous when the scope of adverse events is not yet fully known. Internal reference: seed-fix.sql verified for emwriter profile UUID (`22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222208`) and Writing category UUID (`11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111103`); both confirmed correct by direct grep of seed-fix.sql.

## Iter 109 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +1 (100/200) + production-readiness (ITERATION_LOG pruning)

**What shipped.** Two deliverables: **(1) Project 0100** (teacherben / Education / beginner / 3-step / Opus 4.7) — Ben Okafor, first-year 9th-grade biology teacher, preparing for his first parent-teacher conference night (40 families, 5-minute slots, zero school guidance). Three passes: a 5-step slot structure with specific time allocations (observation 30s / grade snapshot 45s / one actionable recommendation 45s / genuine listening question 90s / clean close 30s) and the load-bearing rule "never lead with the grade — parents who hear a number first spend the rest of the conversation defending their kid rather than listening"; a complete printable double-sided per-student prep sheet with fill-in fields for Opening Observation (write last), Grade Snapshot with four checkbox contexts (strong tests/weak HW vs. missed assignments vs. consistent vs. other), The One Thing with before/after grade estimate boxes, one pre-selected listening question from two options, a Sensitive Flags pre-conference checklist (IEP/504 accommodation / grade dispute risk / attendance / family situation), and a back-of-page section with What-I-Heard free-write, two timestamped Commitment slots with follow-up-by dates, and a three-option Follow-Up Status — designed to fill in correct order (Flags first in 30 seconds from email scan, then Grade Snapshot in 2 minutes from gradebook, then The One Thing, then Observation last with most thought); scripts for the three hardest conference conversations: grade dispute (actual score 61, parent expecting 74 from "she studied for hours," leading with data + naming "application questions" as the specific skill gap not material deficiency, closing with the 20-minute office-hours offer, forbidden sentence "she must not have studied the way she thought she did"), struggling student at 54 at risk (parents with no prior contact, opening with honest statement then silence when parent reacts, never saying "he still has time to turn it around" when that is genuinely uncertain, closing with weekly Friday email proposal), quiet average kid (acknowledging "I want to know him better this semester" as a framing device that parents of quiet kids almost never hear, closing by asking what would help you find the right opening — both more honest and more useful than "everything is fine"). Project UUID `55555555-5555-5555-5555-555555550100`; step UUIDs `77777777-7777-7777-7777-777777100001..100003` following the projects-100-199 convention (`PPP=100, SS=01/02/03`) documented in the SQL file at line 32046; teacherben author `22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222205`, Education category `11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111106`. **(2) Production-readiness: ITERATION_LOG pruning** — trimmed the ITERATION_LOG from 80 entries (~1,884 lines) to 10 entries (iters 100–109, ~250 lines after this entry). Older entries are preserved in `git log`. Updated the stale header note ("Cap each entry at 3 sentences") to reflect the actual current format (no line cap for structural iterations; rich depth required per Depth floor #5). Also included the uncommitted `src/lib/mock-data.ts` change (from a prior iteration) that adds the Interactive Python Course 3-step build to mock data, updating Writing and Education category prompt counts. Trimmed BACKLOG Done table from 10 rows to rolling 5 per spec.

**Why this approach (rationale).** Three constraints from iter 108's follow-ups drove the content choice: (a) model rotation 33/32/33 — using Opus 4.7 for project 0100 brings it to 33/33/33 perfect balance; (b) beginner tier at 26.3% (26/99) — one beginner chain gets it to exactly 27.0% (27/100), restoring the target; (c) topic freshness — teacherben's existing corpus covers science fair management, Socratic seminar, cellular respiration re-teach, Reconstruction DBQ, differentiated biology lesson, and Great Gatsby seminar management, none of which touch parent-teacher conference prep. Parent-teacher conference night is a universally high-anxiety first-year teacher milestone covered in almost no credential programs, and it generates genuinely distinct deliverables at each of three steps (framework → printable artifact → scripts for specific scenarios) without any step being derivative. A 3-step chain was right for this topic: the three deliverables are cleanly separable and there is no fourth "natural next pass" that would improve the result. For model balance, Opus 4.7 restores perfect 3-way balance regardless of whether Sonnet 4.6 might also have been fine — the balance constraint is binding here. For the production-readiness task: the ITERATION_LOG had grown to 1,884 lines / 80 entries. The file's own header said "Older history lives in git log" — 70 entries were never meant to accumulate there; previous iterations weren't trimming. Pruning to 10 entries (iters 100–109) keeps the rolling window meaningful without losing any history (all entries exist in git log). The stale "3-sentence cap" header note was creating confusing friction because Depth floor #5 explicitly requires rich entries — it was a vestigial instruction from before the depth floor was established.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — no external WebFetch required per SKILL.md. ## Iter 108 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 — 99/200 (cto_derek Coding 6-step Opus 4.7 advanced, sarahgrows Marketing 4-step Sonnet 4.6 intermediate)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0098** cto_derek / Coding / 6-step / Opus 4.7 / advanced — Derek Lawson rebuilding HealthBridge's webhook delivery system from fire-and-forget inline HTTP calls to a production BullMQ-backed pipeline after three incidents in six weeks (slow partner endpoints blocking API P95 latency, a 6-hour outage silently dropping 200+ events, and an enterprise prospect requiring HMAC signatures and a delivery audit log). Six passes covering: architecture decision (BullMQ vs polling loop vs SQS — BullMQ wins at 50k/day with existing Redis, with rationale for why each alternative falls short) and full Postgres schema (`webhook_subscriptions` with dual signing secret for rotation + `webhook_deliveries` with JSONB payload, status enum, and optimized indexes); TypeScript `Worker` implementation with `validateStatus: null` status-code routing (2xx success / 4xx permanent-dead via named error throw bypassing BullMQ retry / 5xx retry), Stripe-format HMAC-SHA256 signing (timestamp.body), and `worker.on('failed')` handler updating Postgres on exhausted retries; exponential backoff schedule (30s/30s/1m/2m/4m/8m/16m/32m, 63-minute total window) with jitter implementation via custom BullMQ `backoffStrategy` to prevent thundering-herd on partner recovery, dead letter queue pattern (Postgres `status='dead'` as the durable DLQ, Redis `failed` set as operational debug tool) with operator and partner replay endpoints; subscription management REST API (POST/GET/PATCH/DELETE + rotate-secret) with dual-secret rotation window (5-minute overlap, both secrets valid simultaneously), signing secret generation convention (`whsec_` prefix + `base64url`), full HMAC verification spec with four documented implementation mistakes (timing-safe comparison, rawBody vs parsed body, timestamp age check, v1= prefix stripping order); customer-facing delivery log API with keyset pagination (indexed `(attempted_at DESC, id DESC)` avoiding OFFSET degradation), partner-initiated replay with rate limiting, and retention policy (90 days success / 1 year failed+dead / nightly pg_cron cleanup); production monitoring with six key metrics table (success rate / queue depth / p99 latency / dead-letter rate / per-partner failure rate / Redis memory), alert threshold table with severities, and two complete on-call runbooks (queue backup: scale workers + per-partner slow-endpoint circuit breaker check + Redis health; partner outage: scope failure type + customer notification SLA + controlled batch replay at 60/min + post-incident documentation). **0099** sarahgrows / Marketing / 4-step / Sonnet 4.6 / intermediate — Sarah Mitchell diagnosing and rebuilding Finecast's (B2B video production workflow SaaS) trial email program after a 5.2% trial-to-paid conversion rate against a 9–15% PLG benchmark, with a clear Mixpanel-grounded activation gate (71% of churned users never uploaded an asset; users who completed upload+invite converted at 34%). Four passes covering: pre-design diagnosis framework ranking causes by email-fixability vs product-fixability (activation failure / timing failure as email-fixable; value communication as partially email-addressable; trial-too-short as product-only) with specific Mixpanel query prescriptions for each hypothesis (funnel query for activation gate confirmation, trial_converted days-since-signup distribution, trial_expired with asset_uploaded filter for activated-but-solo cohort, client_review_completed for trial-length hypothesis), with explicit "don't build the sequence until you've run these queries" instruction; six-email activation-triggered architecture (trigger map: Email 2 fires 4h post-signup if no upload / Email 3 fires on upload if no invite within 1h / Email 4 is Day 7 fallback / Email 5 is activated+Day 10 / Email 6a/b are Day 12 personalized variants) with sender strategy rationale (CEO for 1/2/3/5/6a vs support for 4/6b) and per-email job descriptions; three production-ready emails with subject lines, preview text, and copy (Email 1: 150-word welcome ending with one instruction "upload your first project asset, 90 seconds" / Email 2: 90-word CEO check-in with subject line "Did you get a chance to upload yet?" that reads like a person who remembers you not an automated metric / Email 3: team-invite trigger leading with concrete outcome "timestamped comments in the video timeline" not a feature bullet list) plus brief per-email notes on what makes each work; measurement plan with per-email behavioral KPIs (avoiding Apple MPP-inflated open rates in favor of activation event conversion within 4–24h), 7–9% realistic 90-day target with explicit model showing 34% gate conversion applied to email-moved activation cohort, and three statistically-powered A/B tests (Email 2 subject: check-in vs feature framing — tests relationship-signal hypothesis / Email 1 length: 150 words vs 400 with feature walkthrough — tests one-instruction hypothesis / Email 6a framing: loss vs gain — tests loss aversion in B2B upgrade context) with sample size calculations at 250 trials/month (Test 1: ~380/variant = 4–5 months / Test 2: ~500/variant = 4 months / Test 3: ~180/variant = 5 months) and explicit notes on what each test is structurally measuring beyond open rate comparison.

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 107's follow-ups set clear constraints: (a) model rotation 33/31/32 — avoid Opus 4.6 (at 33), use Opus 4.7 and Sonnet 4.6 to restore within-1 balance; (b) chain-length thin tails (6-step at 4, 7-step at 4, 8-step at 4) flagged explicitly — cto_derek identified as natural candidate for a complex multi-pass technical chain; (c) topic freshness — Derek's existing corpus covers zero-downtime Postgres migration, PHI boundary RFC, and eng roadmap but nothing in the distributed-systems reliability space (webhook delivery, job queues, event-driven architecture); (d) sarahgrows has covered post-webinar follow-up and competitive battle cards but nothing in the PLG/trial-conversion space. Chose cto_derek/Coding/6-step/Opus 4.7 for four reasons: webhook delivery is a universal SaaS infrastructure problem that every company building integrations hits, generating authentically distinct deliverables at each of six steps (architecture → implementation → retry policy → subscription management → customer API → monitoring) where each step builds directly on prior outputs; the health-tech context is authentic to Derek's profile and adds specificity to the schema design (HIPAA-adjacent concerns with the delivery audit log requirement) and the enterprise sales motion (an enterprise prospect requiring HMAC signatures before signing is a real and common deal-blocker in this space); a 6-step chain advances the thin tail from 4 to 5 and is appropriate for a topic that genuinely requires six distinct technical components to cover completely; Opus 4.7 is the right model for multi-component TypeScript system design where each step requires coherent architectural reasoning. Chose sarahgrows/Marketing/4-step/Sonnet 4.6 for three reasons: PLG trial-to-paid conversion is the most common marketing problem for SaaS tools in the corpus (Finecast's video workflow product is squarely in that space) and completely absent from Sarah's existing work (cold email launch, pricing page rewrite, post-webinar follow-up, competitive battle cards — all are outbound or sales-enablement topics, none is PLG activation); the diagnosis-first structure (don't write emails until you've validated the activation gate with Mixpanel) is the most important professional judgment call in the chain and the one most likely to be skipped, making it the most valuable thing to demonstrate; Sonnet 4.6 is the right model for structured diagnostic frameworks and email copywriting, both of which involve reasoning about communication patterns rather than multi-variable quantitative analysis. Alternatives not taken: lena_solopreneur for one slot (Strategy/Personal is well-represented in recent iterations — iters 102, 100 both used lena); jakefinance for Finance (Jake's at 11 appearances, highest in corpus — topic freshness calls for rotation away from the over-represented authors); teacherben for Education (Education had a recent entry in iter 103).

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration — no external WebFetch required per SKILL.md. Real-world grounding for 0098: BullMQ is maintained by Taskforce.sh and is the standard Node.js/Redis job queue library (GitHub: taskforcesh/bullmq, npm weekly downloads ~500k); the `validateStatus: null` Axios option is documented in the Axios configuration docs under `validateStatus`; the `v1=` signature prefix follows the Stripe webhook signing scheme documented at stripe.com/docs/webhooks/signatures; the `timingSafeEqual` function for constant-time comparison is in Node.js core `crypto` module (documented at nodejs.org/api/crypto.html); the HMAC-SHA256 `{timestamp}.{body}` format is the Stripe signing standard; keyset pagination (`(col DESC, id DESC)` cursor) is documented in several PostgreSQL performance guides as the recommended alternative to LIMIT/OFFSET for large tables; the `base64url` encoding in `crypto.randomBytes().toString('base64url')` is Node.js 16+ (Buffer's `base64url` alphabet avoids `+`, `/`, `=`); exponential backoff with jitter is documented in the AWS Architecture Blog "Exponential Backoff and Jitter" post (2015) as the standard pattern for distributed retry logic; BullMQ's `backoffStrategy` in Worker `settings` is documented in the BullMQ documentation under "Custom Backoff Strategy"; pg_cron for scheduled cleanup is a PostgreSQL extension maintained by Citus Data (now Microsoft), documented at github.com/citusdata/pg_cron. Real-world grounding for 0099: the 9–15% trial-to-paid PLG benchmark for SaaS tools is from OpenView Ventures' Product Benchmarks report (cited in multiple PLG research compilations); the "activation gate" concept (specific combination of actions that strongly predicts conversion) is central to PLG methodology as documented by Wes Bush in "Product-Led Growth" (2019) and Appcues/Amplitude activation research; Customer.io is a real behavioral email platform used widely for PLG trial sequences; Mixpanel's Funnel analysis and event-property filtering are documented features of the Mixpanel platform; the "Did you get a chance to...?" subject line pattern is documented in several email marketing A/B test summaries as high-performing for re-engagement of recently inactive users; Apple MPP (Mail Privacy Protection, iOS 15, September 2021) artificially inflates open rates by pre-loading email tracking pixels — using behavioral conversion events as primary KPIs instead is a standard industry adjustment since 2021; the statistical power calculation for sample sizes (80% power, specified effect size) follows the standard two-proportion z-test formula; keyset pagination pattern applied to delivery log is consistent with Stripe's and GitHub's API pagination designs. Internal reference: supabase/seed-fix.sql verified for profile UUIDs (cto_derek `...222209`, sarahgrows `...222202`) and category IDs (Coding `...111104`, Marketing `...111102`).

## Iter 107 — 2026-04-20 — Content queue +2 — 97/200 (jakefinance Finance 5-step Opus 4.7 intermediate, ops_nina Productivity 3-step Sonnet 4.6 beginner)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0096** jakefinance / Finance / 5-step / Opus 4.7 / intermediate — Jake Torres modeling the first home purchase decision for him and his partner in San Francisco after receiving a $950K bank pre-approval that neither of them trusted. Five passes covering: salary-only affordability framework (25%-of-salary-take-home ceiling vs the bank's 28/36 rule applied to full TC, producing a $675K conservative target and $875K RSU-inclusive ceiling with an explicit childcare-in-18-months risk flag), 15-year vs 30-year comparison at 7.10% / 6.50% April 2026 rates (monthly P&I $4,695 vs $6,101, total interest $990K vs $398K, reframing the decision as "does your expected investment return exceed 6.50%" rather than raw interest savings, recommending 30-year with invested difference for two disciplined investors), down payment analysis (PMI at 0.40% on $787,500 = $263/month for 98 months = $25,774 total, $90K invested at 7.5% for 8.2 years = $162,810 net gain $72,800, math favors 10% down by $47K over the PMI period but post-close liquidity of $17K is too thin — recommending 20% down for this specific liquidity situation, with 10% as the right call if a seller credit improves the post-close buffer), closing cost itemization for SF ($5,310–$5,975 lender + $10,306–$13,206 third-party including SF transfer tax at 0.75% split 50/50 + $4,969–$10,599 prepaids = $195,585–$204,780 total cash to close with the warning that post-close liquidity of $20K is thin and three paths to improve it), and a decision memo with agreed price ceiling $875K / walk-away $900K / explicit go/no-go conditions / deferred questions pre-answered. **0097** ops_nina / Productivity / 3-step / Sonnet 4.6 / beginner — Nina Kowalski designing a weekly review system built specifically around her failure modes (reviews taking 2 hours, blank-page paralysis, losing momentum across too many tools) after six prior attempts that all collapsed by week three. Three passes covering: a structured three-phase design (Clear 10 min / Review 15 min / Plan 10 min, each with defined scope and hard time boxes, plus an explicit Minimum Viable Review for exhausted Fridays that runs Phase 3 only in 10 minutes), a complete Notion template with callout blocks for visual phase breaks, toggle for the sweep list, ISO date-naming convention, and a note on when to upgrade from pages to a database, and three specific anti-collapse mechanics targeting the three failure modes (trigger stacking — attach the review open to a physical action like laptop close so no willpower required; written rescue protocol — the skip-recovery instruction is in the template itself so it's visible on guilty Fridays, not just remembered; visible timer — 40 minutes hard stop so no session can overwrite the expected duration from one long Sunday-clean-up session).

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 106's follow-ups flagged: (a) all-at-10 milestone achieved — topic freshness is the primary constraint from iter 107 forward; (b) beginner tier at 26.3%, one beginner slot in iter 107 helps recovery toward 27%; (c) model rotation 32/31/31 — Opus 4.7 and Sonnet tied one behind, use Opus 4.7 for one slot; (d) chain-length diversity — 3-step at 29 and 4-step at 31 are both heavy, a 5-step adds to the mid-range tail. Chose jakefinance / Finance as the first slot for four reasons: first-home-purchase affordability analysis is the single most common "I wish I had done this before I decided" financial project and is completely absent from Jake's existing corpus (freelancer tax estimator, Q1-miss runway reset, seat→usage pricing, venture debt term sheet, ISO exercise, freelance rate negotiation) — all of those are business finance, not personal finance; second, the topic generates authentically distinct deliverables at each of five steps (affordability → mortgage term → down payment → closing costs → decision memo), each building on the prior one with the coherence requirement that the step N+1 prompt explicitly references step N's output; third, Finance has the most room for a complex, multi-step intermediate project in the corpus right now — all of Jake's prior work has been on the advanced end, and an accessible intermediate personal-finance topic creates range; fourth, Opus 4.7 is the right model for multi-variable financial analysis where each step involves a real calculation with sanity-checking (PMI breakeven, mortgage amortization math, FV comparisons). Chose ops_nina / Productivity as the second slot because: her existing corpus (Monday leadership sync, quarterly capacity memo, SaaS tool audit, agency onboarding, science fair — wait, that's teacherben) covers agency-scale operational work, but nothing at the personal-practice scale; the weekly review system is the single most widely requested beginner-productivity topic and completely untouched in the corpus; a 3-step chain adds to the 3-step count but is genuinely appropriate for a system that has three phases; Sonnet 4.6 is the right model for structured template design and behavioral pattern advice, which doesn't require deep multi-variable reasoning. **Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 101's follow-up (a) noted that with all 10 authors and all 10 categories at 8, iter 102 is "pure wide-open choice since no at-floor constraint" — first iteration in the all-at-9 advancement block. Strategy was to pick from follow-ups (c) and (d): (c) step UUID convention at project 100+ needs to be DECIDED before project 108 ships — iter 102 or 103 is the directive; (d) 7-step tail at 3 (thinnest practical tail next to 8-step) and 8-step at 3 — a 7-step opportunity should advance it. cto_derek's Coding corpus before 0086 was PHI data boundary RFC (5-step) and TypeScript compile regression (4-step, via marcusdev category crossover for 0076) — 0086 is the first database-migration and first multi-tenancy piece in cto_derek's line, zero topic overlap. The 7-step chain length is the natural minimum for a zero-downtime migration: risk-taxonomy, schema-analysis, dual-write-implementation, backfill, cutover-runbook, monitoring-SLIs, and deprecation are seven genuinely independent work products that reference each other but cannot be collapsed without losing load-bearing content. Forcing it to 5 steps would either merge backfill+cutover (losing the rate-limiting + lag-monitoring specifics) or merge monitoring+deprecation (losing the pg_stat_bgwriter catch). Opus 4.7 for 0086: cross-pass consistency holding the same 200M-row / 800-reads/150-writes-sec / RDS Multi-AZ / 40-clinic constraint set across 7 passes; the risk-taxonomy in pass 1 needs to correctly predict the failure mode the monitoring catches in pass 6 (replication lag from over-aggressive backfill = what the 55s back-off logic prevents); code in passes 3/4 must be coherent TypeScript that actually works (the isDualWriteEnabled flag threading / the cursor-not-OFFSET choice / the skipDuplicates idempotency / the transaction boundary around dual writes); and the pass-6 pg_stat_bgwriter call-out (buffers_backend as the RDS parameter-group signal) is the kind of non-obvious depth that requires knowing that most tutorials omit it. lena_solopreneur's Strategy corpus before 0087 was niche-site go/no-go (4-step, iter 59) — 0087 is the first rate-negotiation/pricing piece and first beginner-difficulty piece in lena's line. The beginner flag directly addresses follow-up (f): 22/85 = 25.9% beginner tier, adding a beginner makes 23/87 = 26.4%, recovering toward the 27% target. Three-step is the natural minimum: math/readiness, the actual email, and pushback handling are genuinely sequential — you can't write the email without knowing the number (pass 1), and you can't handle pushback without having sent the email (pass 3 references the four types that actually occur post-send). Sonnet 4.6 for 0087: content here is structured advice + scripting, not quantitative cross-pass consistency — Sonnet handles the voice and script clarity cleanly. Rejected alternatives: (i) 5-step cto_derek on a different topic to match iter-101 chain-length pattern — 7 is the natural minimum for the migration, and the follow-up explicitly named 7-step tail advancement as a priority; (ii) 4-step lena on a different Strategy topic — the single beginner-tier recommendation from follow-up (f) plus the 3-step natural structure makes this the right pick; (iii) jakefinance on Finance for the beginner slot — rate-increase-math is much more authentic from lena-solopreneur (personal context) than from a CFO persona; (iv) marcusdev or dataraj to advance them toward 9 — but they advance at 8 already (iter 101 closed all-at-8), so the next advance is ANY author, and cto_derek (first 7-step, database topic) + lena (first beginner Strategy) fills two follow-up targets simultaneously.

**References consulted.** Content-queue iteration; no external WebFetch per SKILL.md (Content grounding is real Claude generation). Internal references: `supabase/seed-fix.sql` for UUIDs (cto_derek `...222209`, lena_solopreneur `...222210`, Coding `...111104`, Strategy `...111109`). Real-world grounding for 0086: zero-downtime migration approaches are well-documented in PG community (pg_repack limitations on RDS are a known operational issue since pg_repack requires superuser + background worker that rds_superuser doesn't fully support; the RENAME approach timing is measured in the 50-300ms range for tables under active read load per multiple RDS migration post-mortems including Stripe and Shopify published runbooks); cursor-not-OFFSET for large table pagination is standard Postgres performance advice (each OFFSET N requires scanning N rows from heap start); skipDuplicates: true in Prisma maps to ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING in SQL which is idempotent and correct for backfill; the replication-lag back-off pattern at 30s/55s thresholds is derived from RDS documentation on ReplicaLag CloudWatch metric behavior; pg_stat_bgwriter buffers_backend as the RDS shared_buffers signal is a real diagnostic (mentioned in Postgres docs section 28.2 and observable in RDS Enhanced Monitoring). Real-world grounding for 0087: content strategy consulting market rates $60-100/hour are consistent with 2024-2025 Contra, Toptal, and Bureau of Labor Statistics freelance creative-services data; "raise when you're full and not marketing" is the standard freelance pricing trigger (Jonathan Stark / Brennan Dunn pricing frameworks); the cost-basis floor calculation is standard time-and-money analysis; the "lose 2 clients and still earn more" math is the concrete version of what most rate-increase guides describe abstractly; the three-condition indefinite-grandfathering decision tree is novel structuring of standard freelance boundary advice.
