Next floor goal: "all at 9" — requires 10 more iterations each with 2 projects to advance 20 author-slots and 20 category-slots, so at 2-per-firing that's roughly 10 iterations of balanced advancement. First iteration in that block (iter 102) is pure wide-open choice since no at-floor constraint.
- (b) **115 Content slots remaining; production-readiness pivot at 100 = 15 iterations away** (at 2-per-firing). Pivot trigger is at project 100, not iter 100. Strongly recommend using iter 102-116 to:
  - Continue Content advancement at natural 2-per-firing through slot 100 (iter 107 reaches 97-99 range, iter 108 first to hit 100)
  - Use the 5-6 iters pre-pivot to catch up on chain-length tail advancement (7-step + 8-step still thin at 3 each)
  - Flag the step-UUID-at-project-100 decision (follow-up (j) in iter 100) BEFORE iter 108 which is the first to ship a project at 3-digit index
- (c) **Step-UUID convention at project 100+ still unresolved.** iter 100's flag (j) flagged this as iter 101-117 priority. Current convention `666666XYZW01..` uses 2 decimal digits for project. At 0100 the natural extension would be `666666 + 01 + 00 + 01` for step 1 of project 100 = `666666010001` — this conflicts VISUALLY with projects 01-09 but is UUID-unique. Three options still on the table from iter 100's flag: (i) shift to 3-digit project prefix at 100 (`66666610001` = 11-char not 12, breaks pattern), (ii) use `66666700NN01..` for 100-199 range (different prefix template), (iii) rethink step-UUID generation entirely. Iter 102 or 103 should DECIDE and document the convention in the SQL file header before iter 108 ships. This is mechanical-but-load-bearing — silent inconsistency causes confusion at scale.
- (d) **Chain-length tails after iter 101:** 8-step still at 3, 7-step still at 3, 6-step at 4 (iter 100), 2-step at 2 (chronic thin). Middle: 4-step ~16, 5-step ~18, 3-step ~26 (densest). Iter 101 added middle-lengths (4 + 5). Next iter should look at 7-step or 8-step opportunistic advance if natural fit appears.
- (e) **Model rotation 27/28/27 → 28/28/28 PERFECT 3-way balance.** Iter 101 achieves second perfect-balance point in corpus (first was iter 98). Iter 102 any model pick maintains within-1. No rotation pressure.
- (f) **Beginner tier drifted 22/83 = 26.5% → 22/85 = 25.9%.** Target 27% now ~1.1 percentage points below. If iter 102 picks a beginner, becomes 23/87 = 26.4%. If iter 102+103 both include a beginner, reaches 24/89 = 27.0%. Recommendation: iter 102 include 1 beginner if natural fit found; flag for subsequent iters if not.
- (g) **Quality observation on 0084:** the single most-load-bearing reframe was "this isn't 'are we running the wrong webinars' it's 'is the follow-up broken'" — the VP-facing narrative switch that let the marketer walk out of the Q1 review with a path-forward instead of a defensive posture. Pattern: when a cross-functional metric miss is on the table, the first 5 minutes of the meeting determines whether you're defending the whole strategy or rebuilding one piece of it. Flag for future Marketing / Strategy / cross-functional-communication content to always include a "what's the load-bearing reframe" line.
- (h) **Quality observation on 0085:** the pass-4 acquihire-below-preference scenario is the case most engineers don't model — the cross-functional literature (Holloway, Secfi) collapses this to "bad outcome" without walking through the after-tax math showing Path A LOSES MORE in that scenario than Path B. The 4-scenario × 2-path table that makes the delta numerically visible is genuinely load-bearing in changing the decision. Pattern: any decision framework with asymmetric downside must include a quantitative walk-through of the downside scenarios, not just "and also bad outcomes can happen." Flag for future equity / finance / quantitative-decision content.
- (i) **Quality observation on 0085 pass 3:** the 83(b) mechanics pass is the kind of content where "the $15 and 3 hours has the highest leverage ratio of anything in your financial life this year" framing is what drives behavior change from "I'll figure it out" to "I'll upgrade to certified mail today." Pattern: for mechanical-but-high-stakes processes, explicit cost-of-being-careful vs cost-of-failure math is the load-bearing frame that moves readers from "I know I should" to actually doing it. Flag for future process-compliance / legal-adjacent / irreversible-deadline content.
- (j) **mock-data.ts uncommitted Drew work continues orphaned** — now 17 iterations old (iter 84-101). 15 iters to production-readiness pivot. Still strongly recommend Drew review before pivot or the production-readiness queue will inherit a murky diff.
- (k) **Iter 101 word count:** ~12,800 words total (0084 ~5,600 + 0085 ~7,200). Under iter-100's 14,500-word and iter-98's 17,700-word ceilings. 4-step + 5-step pairing fits depth floor cleanly.
- (l) **Difficulty distribution post-101:** beginner 22/85 = 25.9%, intermediate ~47/85 = 55.3%, advanced ~16/85 = 18.8%. Intermediate tier dominates by design. Advanced tier at 18.8% — within acceptable 15-25% band for a mixed-skill corpus.

## Iter 100 — 2026-04-19 — Content queue +2 — 83/200 (dataraj Data 6-step Opus 4.7 advanced, lena_solopreneur Personal 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate)

**What shipped.** Appended two projects to `supabase/seed-content-chains.sql`: **0082** dataraj / Data / 6-step Opus 4.7 advanced — senior data analyst at a 110-person SaaS company catches a $1.8M pipeline variance 96 hours before CFO quotes the number to the board; six passes covering triage plan (5 checks ordered frequency-weighted with filter-parity first + duplicate second + stage-integrity third + time budgets per check + pre-emptive escalation decision tree "never surprise the CFO on Thursday"), Snowflake SQL for parent-child duplicate detection (group-root resolution + 3 suspicion tiers + mirror-pair elimination + 5-point manual review rubric + renewal-vs-duplicate gotcha), Stage-5 artifact-score SQL with 4-artifact checklist + politics rules "you are Data not Sales — report artifacts not behaviors / route through regional VPs / expect pushback and prepare", confidence-band construction via RSS of 4 independent uncertainty sources arriving at ±$180K + one-pager memo structure with "**none represent lost revenue, only miscounted records**" as the single most-load-bearing reframing line, board-deck language with ≈ signaling + 5 anticipated Q&A each answered in ≤2 sentences + "I don't know" three-words protocol + half-beat-pause-when-CFO-asks-you rule, and 4-part post-audit governance (scope boundary explicitly written "in scope / out of scope" / nightly duplicate-alerting dbt + Slack / Salesforce validation rule blocking artifact-less Stage-5 + override audit trail / monthly Snowflake-SFDC reconciliation / quarterly codified audit as standing deliverable / 4-tile dashboard + "what this system will NOT catch" honesty appendix). Result notes the revised $6.74M number held in board meeting with no blowups, Q4-style questions about governance came up and CFO used Claude's answer nearly verbatim, governance plan is now standing infra two quarters in. **0083** lena_solopreneur / Personal / 4-step Opus 4.6 intermediate — Brooklyn freelance copy editor with 120 active clients (3 publisher retainers) given 9 weeks to move cross-country to Seattle for partner's UW job; four passes covering 9-week transition framework (name-the-3-assets-you're-protecting + measurable-definition-of-maintain = 3 numbers / ≥90% retention / retainers intact / 8+ inquiries per month months 1-3 + what-stays-same-vs-what-actually-changes + "when does a client need to know" 3-criteria filter + default-heuristic "don't tell the client" as antidote to over-communication instinct + anti-pattern "don't use your client list as group-therapy audience — save a Drafts-folder draft for processing"), 3-tier client segmentation by "how much would 10-day window affect them" not "how much do they pay" (5-10 Tier-A personal-heads-up with lead-with-concrete-plan-not-apology scripts / 25-35 Tier-B generic "personal logistics" don't-say-Seattle 75-word template / 75-90 Tier-C no-communication + publisher-retainer phone-calls-not-emails + "no mass-BCC I'm-excited-to-announce" anti-pattern), 10-day day-by-day move-week operational plan (twice-daily 15-min email triage / phone-OOO "urgent-matters-only" / "real emergency" pre-defined 3-category protocol / NO VA + NO email auto-forward + NO temporary editor-handling-client-work rules each with rationale / 1-page emergency-contact-card / "Sep 11 I'm back" pre-written pre-scheduled email as a surprisingly-load-bearing move / the-10-day-window-is-structural-not-heroic close), and 90-day Seattle rebuild plan (Weeks 1-4 stability with WA B&O-tax-not-income specifics + accountant consult $200 + back-to-full-availability batch-email / Weeks 4-8 3-targeted-local-moves 8-12-named-agents-and-presses + ONE-local-community-of-practice NWIEG-or-PNWA + re-engage-ONE-dormant-NYC-asset NOT-generic-Seattle-mixers / Weeks 8-12 first-Seattle-delivery + ONE-recurring-coffee + re-segment-client-list / real-vs-vanity metrics / "at week 3 your inbox will be quiet — it's NOT collapsing" prep / write-80-20-diversification-line-NOW-and-reread-in-December-when-homesick / 500-word-2-year-reflection-for-yourself-don't-publish). Result notes 5.8% churn (within <10% plan), all 3 retainers intact, month-4 revenue at 94% of pre-move baseline, business is structurally healthier a year in (80/20 East/West diversification).

**Why this approach (rationale).** Iter 99 follow-up gave clean guidance: (b) 4 categories at 7 (Finance / Marketing / Data / Personal) vs 6 at 8 — iter 100 should pick from the 4-at-7 to keep the 7→8 advance moving and close toward "all-at-8"; (c) 4 authors at 7 (dataraj / sarahgrows / marcusdev / lena) — any 2 pairings work; (d) 6-step tail at 3 is thin, opportunistic long-chain pick natural; (e) model rotation 27/27/26 — picking 1 Opus 4.7 re-tightens to 27/27/27; (f) beginner tier crossed 27% target, tier-agnostic OK. dataraj + lena pairing hits all four: 6-step phantom-pipeline audit advances Data 7→8 AND dataraj 7→8 AND Opus 4.7 balance AND 6-step tail 3→4 AND is fresh ground (prior dataraj: cohort retention 5-step, A/B test lift investigation 4-step, live MRR variance 5-step, customer-churn post-acquisition 4-step, warehouse consolidation 6-step, SaaS-retention-cohort calc 4-step, fraud-model drift 3-step — zero Salesforce-pipeline-audit, zero data-quality-for-board-prep, zero CFO-politics territory); 4-step cross-country-move advances Personal 7→8 AND lena 7→8 AND is fresh (prior lena: Sequoia camping 3-step, niche-site sunset 4-step, rescue-dog decision 3-step, bootstrap strategy 4-step, daughter-scholarship 3-step, DC mother death estate 5-step, job-to-freelance transition 4-step — zero cross-country-move, zero service-business-through-relocation, zero client-continuity-with-120-relationships). Model rotation: Opus 4.7 for 6-step pipeline audit (capability justified — 6 passes of data-quality methodology + political framing + board-room prep, each pass has to hold the prior passes' findings in memory and respond to specific CFO fears, plus pass 5 required Claude to push back on the "say you don't know" reflex with a structured protocol not a truism), Opus 4.6 for 4-step relocation framework (judgment-heavy service-business reasoning — pass 1's "don't tell most clients" conclusion is counterintuitive and required Opus depth to justify against the transparency default, pass 2's tier-segmentation required real distinctions between "similar amount of attention"-tier-A vs "similar overall revenue"-tier that Sonnet would have collapsed, pass 3 required naming specific anti-patterns like "no VA" with 3 reasons each, pass 4 required both numeric metrics and the philosophical "80/20 diversification" frame). Rejected alternatives: (i) sarahgrows + marcusdev — sarahgrows/Marketing advance possible and marcusdev is Coding-already-at-8 forcing cross-category assignment (weaker fit); dataraj+lena keeps author→category matched cleanly; (ii) 3-step Sonnet for lena — would collapse the 4-stage temporal arc (framework / segmentation / move-week / 90-day) into fewer passes losing the distinctness of each phase; 4-step is natural minimum; (iii) 8-step for dataraj to hit deepest tail — pipeline audit is genuinely 6-beat (triage / duplicates / stage / reconstruct / brief / govern); padding to 8 would add cadence without content; (iv) beginner tier for lena — cross-country-with-120-clients requires intermediate craft judgment, forcing beginner would produce generic moving advice not the service-business-specific framework needed; (v) marcusdev/Personal on a generic-dev topic — would create cross-category fit that's weaker than keeping dataraj-Data and lena-Personal matched. Topic choices: data-quality-audit-before-board-meeting is the archetypal data-leadership test case every analyst faces (even if the $1.8M specifics differ, the pattern of "you caught something 4 days before your boss quotes a number" is universal in data roles), and the political dimension ("you are Data not Sales") is the single most-undertreated topic in public data-analytics writing; cross-country-move-with-service-business maps to a real scarcity in self-employment content (generic moving guides are abundant, service-business-through-relocation guides with actual segmentation math are not) and the "don't tell most clients" reframe is load-bearing enough that it alone justifies the project.

- (h) **Quality observation on 0082:** the single highest-leverage line in pass 4 was "none represent lost revenue, only miscounted records" — the reframe that let the CFO walk into the board meeting confident instead of defensive. Future boardroom / finance-adjacent content should always include the "what reframe does your reader need to lead with" question explicitly. It's a pattern that generalizes (any time someone is about to communicate bad-looking data to their boss, the question is "what frame does your boss need to not feel blindsided"). Flag for inclusion in future Strategy / Productivity / ops-sensitive chains.
- (i) **Quality observation on 0083:** the "save a Drafts-folder draft for processing, leave it there" anti-pattern callout is the kind of unexpected-but-useful specific that elevates a project above generic how-to content. Future relocation / life-transition / change-management content should include at least one "here is the thing you'll be tempted to do that you should not do, and here is the substitute" callout. Pattern: name-the-anti-pattern + offer-a-cheap-substitute beats "don't do X" alone because the reader needs to discharge the underlying impulse somewhere.
- (j) **Step-ID allocation approaching 2-digit project-prefix limit.** Current convention `666666XYZW01..` uses 2 decimal digits for project. 0082 → `82`, 0083 → `83` all fine through 99. At project 100+, the convention breaks (`666666 + 10001 + 01 = 66666610001 01` is 13 chars vs. the UUID's 12-char slot). Iter 101-117 should decide: (i) shift step-UUIDs to 3-digit project prefix at 100 (breaks convention visually but keeps clean structure); (ii) use different prefix template from 100+ (e.g., `66666700NN01..` for 100-199 range); (iii) rethink step-UUID generation entirely. Flag priority for iter 101 or iter 102 — decide before project 100 ships.
